| 108| AZW3/Foliate reader: center tap does not toggle chrome (REOPENED 2026-05-20 — regression)             | Foliate/* | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-21 (v3.39.1, branch `fix/issue-224-azw3-center-tap-chrome`)** — root cause was a coordinate-space mismatch introduced by the Bug #239 fix (`bd7564c7`), NOT the bilingual-injection hypothesis in the original reopen note (device diagnosis confirmed the bilingual path does in-place DOM `insertBefore` and never reloads the doc; the click listener already re-binds on every Foliate `load`). In **paginated** mode foliate-js renders a section as a 2-column page inside an iframe ~2× the screen width and pages by shifting that iframe horizontally via its element `left` (device-confirmed: `left: -359` over a 402px host viewport) to reveal one column. The Bug #239 content-tap handler posted `{x: event.clientX, w: documentElement.clientWidth}` — but `event.clientX` is in the iframe's internal coordinate space (0..748) while `documentElement.clientWidth` is a single column (374). So `ReaderTapZoneRouter` saw `x/w ∈ ~1.0..2.0` on every right-column page and classified a center tap as a right-zone tap → `.readerNextPage` instead of `.readerContentTapped`; the toolbar never toggled (and on the right edge the tap turned the page). EPUB was unaffected because it renders in the top-level document (no nested iframe → `clientX`/`clientWidth` already host-relative). **Fix**: new `mapTapToHostViewport(doc, clientX)` in `foliate-host.js` maps the click back to host-viewport coords — `hostX = clientX + frameElement.getBoundingClientRect().left`, `hostW = frameElement.ownerDocument.defaultView.innerWidth`; no host frame → `documentElement.clientWidth` (top-level case); unusable host width / cross-origin → returns `null` so the handler posts the bare chrome-toggle `tap` (safe default). `foliate-bundle.js` rebuilt via `build-bundle.sh`. **Device-verified (iPhone 17 Pro Sim iOS 26.5, UDID `1FAB9493…`, mini-azw3 paginated, right-column page `frameLeft=-359`)**: the live production handler, captured via the real `webkit.messageHandlers.tap.postMessage`, posts `{x:201,w:402}` for a screen-center tap → `0.50` → center/TOGGLE; screen-left(15%) → `{x:60,w:402}` → left/prev; screen-right(85%) → `{x:341,w:402}` → right/next (Bug #239 side-tap preserved). Regression guard `FoliateHostTapCoordinateTests` pins both source + built bundle with comment-stripped executable-pattern assertions. Codex Gate-4 audit: 2 rounds, ship-as-is (`.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-224-azw3-center-tap-chrome-audit.md`). **REOPENED 2026-05-20 (user triage — "can not see the tool bar by tapping on the center")**. The original fix (FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator's `handleMessage(name:"tap")` posting `.readerContentTapped`) IS still in place at `vreader/Views/Reader/FoliateSpikeView.swift:617-623`; the JS producer is still at `vreader/Services/Foliate/JS/foliate-host.js:120` (`post('tap', {})` from a doc-level `click` listener attached on `view.addEventListener('load', ...)`). User reports center-tap no longer toggles the toolbar on AZW3. Strong suspect: feature #56 WI-11 (`e8c1c2e4` — `FoliateBilingualContainerView`) or WI-15 (`5adc346b` — re-translation) injection breaks the click-listener chain. The bilingual JS injects `<div class="vreader-bilingual" data-vreader-decoration>` blocks after each source paragraph; if injection reloads or replaces the doc, the `click` listener (attached once at `view.load`) does not re-attach to the new doc and the `post('tap', {})` never fires. Cross-ref: Bug #246 (AZW3 wrong-reader-UI) filed concurrently — if both share root cause, Bug #246's fix lands first and #108's repro should be retested. **Fix direction**: re-bind the doc-level click listener every time the Foliate view emits a `load` event (not just on initial), OR delegate the click capture to a higher-level listener that survives doc replacement. **Original fix history (still valid as a contract)**: Toolbar stayed visible on center tap in FoliateSpikeView (the AZW3 reader). EPUB chrome toggle worked. **FIXED** by adding `case "tap":` to FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator's message handler that posts `.readerContentTapped` — the notification ReaderContainerView already observes to call `toggleChrome()`. Root cause: the JS bundle's `tap` message hit the default branch and no-oped. Refactored: extracted Coordinator from inside `FoliateSpikeWebView` (private struct) into a top-level extension so the new `handleMessage(name:body:)` method is unit-testable without constructing a real `WKScriptMessage`. Verified by `FoliateSpikeViewTapTests.tapMessage_postsReaderContentTappedNotification`. Codex audit: 1 round + 1 followup, ship-as-is. GH: #224 |

| 146| Late-attached observer misses debugBridgeThemeChanged on reader-mount                                 | DevTools/*| Low      | WONT FIX    | Originally filed by Codex audit on bug #144 fix as a theoretical first-mount race. **Re-investigated 2026-05-06; not a real race** — `RealDebugBridgeContext.theme(_:_:)` writes UserDefaults BEFORE posting the notification (via `store.theme = target` whose `didSet` calls `defaults.set`). When a fresh `ReaderContainerView` mounts, its `@State settingsStore = ReaderSettingsStore()` initializer reads UserDefaults at view-init — which already has the new value. The "missed notification" is redundant for a fresh-mount case. UserDefaults is the source of truth at init; the notification is a live-update primitive for an EXISTING reader. Reconcile-from-defaults safety net was prototyped on `fix/issue-320-reconcile-from-defaults` and reverted unmerged after this analysis: the simulated race didn't actually demonstrate the fix because UserDefaults backstops the scenario. Closing as WONT FIX. GH: #320 |

| 148| `decodeWithHint_fallsBack_whenHintEncodingFailsToDecode` test broken: 24-byte UTF-8 input is even-length, so UTF-16 hint silently decodes to gibberish | Reader/*  | Low      | FIXED       | **FIXED**: test renamed `..._whenHintEncodingIsUnknown` and rewritten to trigger the fallback via `encodingFromName` returning nil (unknown hint name "ZZZ-NotReal") instead of via decoder-rejects-bytes. Foundation's `String(data:, encoding: .utf16)` is lenient: it accepts any even-byte payload (silently drops trailing odd byte) and returns UTF-16 code units regardless of content, so the original premise (odd-byte input → UTF-16 returns nil) was wrong — a 13-byte payload still decoded to 6 chars. The unknown-name path is the only reliable trigger for the fallback in a unit test. Added `#expect(encodingFromName(hintName) == nil)` guard so future aliasing fails loudly. Codex audit: 2 rounds, ship-as-is. Both Lows (rename for accuracy + aliasing guard) addressed in round 2. GH: #338 |

Findings (paraphrased): (1) Foliate's `loadHTMLString` finishes before foliate-js parses the book, so `isLoading == false` does not imply rendered — misses criterion (d); (2) EPUB does post-`didFinish` work (150ms restored-scroll, 200ms pagination query) so polling can return before the visible state is committed; transient `isLoading == false` during intra-book transitions can also false-positive. **Real fix needs a per-bridge "render-complete" signal** fired after the render genuinely completes. **SETTLE PORTION FIXED** in the `fix/issue-305-debugbridge-settle-strategy` PR: `DebugReaderRegistry+Settle.swift` (new) adds `markReaderSettled(for:token:)` + `awaitReaderSettled(for:token:timeout:)` — a render-settled signal keyed by `(fingerprintKey, token)` with the same UUID-token waiter machinery + `expectedReaderToken` stale-write guard as `awaitReader`. EPUB marks settled from `EPUBWebViewBridge.Coordinator.webView(_:didFinish:)` (page-load complete); AZW3/MOBI from the Foliate `relocate` message (`FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator` — the live host — gained a `relocate` case; `FoliateViewCoordinator`'s existing `relocate` case also marks). `relocate` is the real render-complete signal — `didFinish` is just the HTML shell before foliate-js paginates. `ReaderContainerView.onAppear` wires `probe.settleStrategy` for `.epub`/`.azw3`; TXT/MD/PDF keep the 100ms `Task.sleep` fallback (out of scope). Settled state cleared in `unregister(_:)` (with `preservingToken` so a same-key reopen doesn't clobber the incoming reader's state) + `reset()`. 17 settle tests (Core/Cleanup/EdgeCase suites) + 3 adapter tests. | 135| EPUBHighlightBridge.jsEscape misses U+2028/U+2029/tab — search-highlight breaks on legit CJK separators | EPUB/*   | Low      | FIXED       | Found during feature #11 verification 2026-05-06. `EPUBHighlightBridge`'s private `jsEscape` covered only `\\`, `'`, `"`, `\n`, `\r` — missing `\t`, U+2028 (LINE SEPARATOR), U+2029 (PARAGRAPH SEPARATOR). The latter two are ECMAScript line terminators that break single-quoted string literals; legitimate in some CJK ebooks. `searchHighlightJS` interpolates user-controlled `textQuote` directly, so a search query containing one would produce a SyntaxError → `window.find` never runs → highlight silently fails. **FIXED** by replacing the private helper with a delegating call to the shared `FoliateJSEscaper.escapeForJSString` (single source of truth, vetted impl). | 152| `TestSeeder` doesn't clear UserDefaults across `--uitesting` launches; OPDS / per-book / theme / AI-consent state persists | DevTools/*| Low      | FIXED    | **Filed by verify cron 2026-05-08T08:40** during feature #36 (OPDS catalog) round-2 verification attempt. UserDefaults state (OPDS catalog list, library sort/view-mode preferences, reader theme/fontSize/lineSpacing/paged-mode toggle, AI consent flags, per-book settings cache) is NOT reset on `--uitesting` (which only swaps the SwiftData store for an in-memory container). Verified end-to-end: `OPDSCatalogListTests.testOPDSEmptyStateWithResetPreferences` (uses `resetPreferences: true`) deterministically asserts the OPDS empty-state shape now passes. 8 new unit tests in `TestSeederPreferencesTests` cover per-subsystem clear, leaves-unrelated-keys-untouched, idempotency, and a drift gate vs `BackupSettingsKeys.all`. | 153| Search-result-tap navigation places matched text above viewport; highlight invisible before 3s auto-clear | Reader/*  | Medium   | FIXED    | **Filed by verify cron 2026-05-08T13:45** during feature #5 (Search highlight auto-dismiss) device verification with computer-use. Distinct from `attemptScrollRestore` (saved-position resume — top edge is correct there). 7 new pure-logic unit tests cover the headroom math; CU-driven repro on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.85 — search "100" → tap result → "Paragraph 100" line is fully visible in the viewport (was previously off-screen above). | 154| Search-tap navigation in TXT reader skips temporary yellow highlight at destination (bug #43 contract regression) | Reader/*  | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-19** (branch `fix/issue-443-search-nav-highlight-renav`). Implements the runtime-traced root cause from the 2026-05-18 trace below: a search-nav to an already-current target re-sets `uiState.highlightRange` / `scrollToOffset` to values they already hold → `@Observable` no-op write → SwiftUI body never re-evaluates → bridge `updateUIView` never runs → temp highlight never re-painted. **Fix**: added a monotonic `highlightNonce: Int` to `TextReaderUIState` (and the `ReaderNotificationHandlerStateProtocol`), bumped on every navigate event by `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleNavigateToLocator` (`&+=`, after the nil-offset guard). `TXTTextViewBridge` + `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` fold a nonce change into their highlight-change detection via the new pure static `TXTTextViewBridge.highlightShouldReapply(rangeChanged:nonceChanged:)`, so a repeat-nav re-paints + re-arms the 3 s auto-clear timer even when the NSRange is byte-for-byte identical. `ReaderNotificationModifier` was switched from a duplicate inline copy of the navigate logic to call the extracted, unit-tested `handleNavigateToLocator` (removes the duplication that caused the nonce bump to be missed). Next bugfix iteration must trace the notification → uiState → bridge round-trip with logging at each stage. Original PARTIAL FIX context preserved below. — **PARTIAL FIX SHIPPED** in earlier PR: orphan `@State` in `TXTReaderContainerView.swift` removed; `readerContent` (line 472) + `chunkedReaderContent` (line 527) now wired to `uiState.highlightRange` / `uiState.highlightIsTemporary`. 4 regression-guard tests in `vreaderTests/Views/Reader/TXTReaderContainerSearchHighlightWiringTests.swift` pin the wiring contract. **Runtime symptom on Position Test Book NOT yet gone** because Position Test Book triggers chapter mode (`hasChapterDisplay = true` via detected `Section N` markers), and `chapterReaderContent` (line 496) intentionally hardcodes `highlightRange: nil // Highlight offset translation is WI-7`. All 3 WIs of feature #48 now on main. Full code fix complete; device verification pending (awaiting-device-verification label remains until GH close). The original verify-cron analysis conflated two distinct concerns: (a) orphan `@State` in non-chapter paths (real, this PR addresses, with regression-guard tests); (b) WI-7 chapter-mode global→local offset translation (deferred feature work, no fixture yet exercises the non-chapter paths to runtime-verify (a) directly). MD reader is unaffected because MD does not have a chapter-mode renderer branch. **Filed by verify cron 2026-05-08T22:57** during feature #2 (Highlight search result at destination) round-2 verification. Sibling to bug #153: while #153 fixed the SCROLL POSITION (matched text now lands inside the viewport with 25% top headroom), the temporary yellow highlight on the matched range itself NEVER renders for TXT files. Reproducible end-to-end on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.92: launch with `--seed-position-test --reset-preferences`, open Position Test Book, tap search → paste "Paragraph 50" → tap result. Reader scrolls correctly to paragraph 50 (#153 fix working), but no `UIColor.systemYellow.withAlphaComponent(0.4)` background appears on "Paragraph 50" before the 3s auto-clear timer would fire. Two artifacts saved (`feature-2-r2-after-search-tap-paragraph50-20260508.png` + `feature-2-r2-immediately-after-tap-20260508.png`). Root cause (code-read confirmed): `TXTReaderContainerView.swift` declares two `highlightRange` states — line 62 has a local `@State private var highlightRange: NSRange?` that's read by `readerContent` (line 471) and `chapterReaderContent` (line 526) but **never assigned anywhere**, while line 78's `@State var uiState = TextReaderUIState()` exposes `uiState.highlightRange` (the one `ReaderNotificationModifier.swift:34-47` actually sets when `.readerNavigateToLocator` fires). `MDReaderContainerView.swift:312` reads `uiState.highlightRange` (correct wiring); the TXT container reads the orphan local @State. Net effect: search-tap notification updates `uiState.highlightRange`, but `TXTTextViewBridge` is fed the orphan `@State` so `applyHighlights` is a no-op for the active range. Affects every TXT search; PDF/EPUB/Foliate paths use their own renderer and are not affected. Fix sketch: delete the orphan `@State` at lines 62 + 65, replace `highlightRange: highlightRange` and `highlightIsTemporary: highlightIsTemporary` at 471/472 + 526/527 with `uiState.highlightRange` / `uiState.highlightIsTemporary`. Add an integration test asserting that posting `.readerNavigateToLocator` with a TXT locator results in the bridge's active highlight range matching the locator's `charRangeStartUTF16/charRangeEndUTF16`. Cross-ref: feature #2 evidence at `dev-docs/verification/feature-2-20260508.md`. **Bugfix-cron diagnostic round 2026-05-18** (deep code-read responding to the REOPENED note's "trace the round-trip" mandate — no runtime trace yet, no code shipped). **(1) Range translation PROVEN correct, ruled OUT as the cause**: within a single `chapterReaderContent` render (`TXTReaderContainerView.swift:569`), `chapterLocalScrollOffset` and `chapterLocalHighlightRanges` take the *same* `viewModel.currentChapterIdx` + chapters, and `uiState.scrollToOffset == uiState.highlightRange.location` (both = `resolveTXT`'s `globalStart` — `SearchHitToLocatorResolver.resolveTXT` sets `charOffsetUTF16 == charRangeStartUTF16 == segBase + matchStart`, `ReaderNotificationModifier:37-42` copies them). So scroll-translation-succeeds ⟹ highlight-temp-translation-succeeds in that render; `TXTChapterHighlightHelper.highlightsForChapter`'s clip math is sound. The symptom "scroll works, highlight doesn't" therefore is NOT the global→chapter-local translation. **(2) Concrete defect found — `TXTTextViewBridge.makeUIView`**: it seeds `coordinator.persistedHighlights` from the param (`TXTTextViewBridge.swift:101`) but does NOT seed `coordinator.currentHighlightRange` from the `highlightRange` param. `makeUIView`'s initial `applyHighlights` (line 108, commented "set highlights first so drawBackground has correct ranges") thus paints `active: nil` — the temp/search highlight is dropped on a fresh bridge's first render. **(3) Why chapter-mode-specific**: chapter-mode search-nav swaps `chapterAttrString` nil→loadingView→back (`TXTReaderContainerView.swift:595-601`), so SwiftUI creates a FRESH `TXTTextViewBridge` per chapter (fresh coordinator, `currentHighlightRange` defaults nil). Non-chapter `readerContent`/`chunkedReaderContent` keep ONE bridge identity for the whole doc, so their `updateUIView` always carries the highlight — that is why TXT-non-chapter + MD are unaffected. **(4) Not yet pinned**: whether seeding `currentHighlightRange` in `makeUIView` (symmetric with line 101) is the *complete* fix, or whether a second `updateUIView` highlightChanged-timing factor remains — needs the `Logger` runtime trace of `makeUIView`/`updateUIView`/`chapterReaderContent` against `--seed-position-test` that the REOPENED note asked for. **Do NOT ship a code-read-only fix** — this bug was already twice "code-complete but runtime-incomplete" (PARTIAL FIX, then WI-3); the next bugfix iteration must runtime-trace first, then fix + RED/GREEN test + device-verify. Status stays REOPENED. **Bugfix-cron runtime trace 2026-05-18 (the mandated trace — DONE; supersedes diagnoses (1)-(4) above).** Instrumented `Logger` traces across the full chain (`readerNavigateToLocator`→`chapterLocalHighlightRanges`→`updateUIView`→`setHighlightRanges`→`HighlightingLayoutManager.drawBackground`), built + installed on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4), ran the `--seed-position-test` repro 3×. **Finding A — the highlight DOES render; the makeUIView-asymmetry hypothesis (2) is WRONG.** Run 1 (first search-tap, reader scrolls top→Para 50): the full chain fires — `chapterLocalHighlightRanges tempGlobalRange={8847,12} chapterIndex=0 → temp={8847,12}` (chapter translation correct, confirming (1)); `updateUIView highlightChanged=true`; `setHighlightRanges active={8847,12} numberOfGlyphs=18027`; then `drawBackground searchHighlightRange={8847,12} … visibleGlyphIntersect.len=12` (the `paint()` yellow-fill *executes*); then `setHighlightRanges active=nil` exactly 3.0s later (auto-clear timer). The temporary highlight renders correctly for the full 3s window. `makeUIView` runs once at app launch with `highlightRange=nil`; search-nav is delivered via `updateUIView` which seeds + paints correctly — so the `makeUIView`/`currentHighlightRange` asymmetry is a harmless latent inconsistency, NOT this bug. **Finding B — the real defect: a repeat-nav produces no view update.** Runs 2 & 3 (re-tap the same search result while the reader is ALREADY at that location): `readerNavigateToLocator` fires and re-sets `uiState.highlightRange={8847,12}` — but **zero downstream chain** (no `chapterLocalHighlightRanges`/`updateUIView`/`setHighlightRanges`/`drawBackground` logged at all). Cause: the `.readerNavigateToLocator` handler (`ReaderNotificationModifier.swift:37-46`) sets `uiState.scrollToOffset` / `highlightIsTemporary` / `highlightRange` all to the values they ALREADY hold — the prior nav left them set, and the 3s auto-clear clears only the bridge coordinator's `currentHighlightRange`, never `uiState.highlightRange`. With no observable change, `TXTReaderContainerView.body` does not re-evaluate → `updateUIView` is never called → the temp highlight is never re-applied. Run 1 only worked because the SCROLL itself drove the re-render. **Why verify-cron repeatedly saw "no highlight":** (a) computer-use screenshots taken via a model round-trip after the tap routinely land *past* the 3s auto-clear window — reproduced exactly in this round's run 1 (screenshot at tap+~4s, highlight already cleared); and/or (b) repeated repro attempts on the same paragraph (round-2: 4 attempts; round-3: re-ran "Paragraph 50"/"Paragraph 100") hit Finding B from the 2nd attempt onward. **Corrected root cause:** the bug is real, but the trigger is "search-nav to an already-current target," NOT "first search." The filed first-search repro is not itself a product defect — it is a screenshot-timing artifact. **Fix direction (NOT shipped this iteration):** make the temporary search highlight re-apply on every `.readerNavigateToLocator` regardless of whether `uiState` values changed — e.g. a monotonic nonce on `TextReaderUIState` bumped by the handler and treated like `highlightChanged` by the TXT/chunked/MD bridges, and/or have the 3s auto-clear also clear `uiState.highlightRange` so a re-nav becomes a genuine nil→value transition. Cross-cutting (`TextReaderUIState` + `ReaderNotificationModifier` + `TXTTextViewBridge` + `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` + `MDReaderContainerView`) — a proper multi-file TDD fix, not a patch. This iteration ran the mandated trace only; no code shipped (instrumentation reverted, fix branch dropped); the CU display went unavailable mid-session so a behavioral UI fix cannot be device-verified now — fix deferred to a future bugfix iteration. Status stays REOPENED. GH: #443 |

| 171| EPUB paged mode shows two-column layout instead of single-page flip on iPhone 17 Pro | Reader/EPUB | High | FIXED | **Filed by user 2026-05-12** (GH issue created 2026-05-12). Repro: open any EPUB → enable Paged layout → two text columns appear side-by-side instead of a single page-flip layout like Kindle/Apple Books. **Root cause** (code-read confirmed at `vreader/Views/Reader/EPUBPaginationHelper.swift:31`): `paginationCSS(viewportWidth:viewportHeight:)` set `column-width: (viewportWidth - 40)px` without enforcing `column-count`. CSS `column-width` is a **hint** (minimum desired width) — the browser creates as many columns as fit. When the viewport width / book CSS combination allowed two columns to fit (e.g. book stylesheet pushed body width beyond the viewport), the browser packed two columns. **FIXED 2026-05-12**: added `column-count: 1 !important` to the body CSS. Round-1 audit (Codex thread `019e1827-04bd-7593-96a1-59f78fea2030`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is) escalated the defense to mark the FULL pagination param set reader-owned via `!important` (column-count, column-width, column-gap, column-fill, height, and html+body overflow) — so book CSS `!important` on column-width or height can't desynchronize `scrollWidth / viewportWidth` and break paging math. Round-1 finding [3] also tightened a pre-existing tiny-viewport gap: `column-width` and `height` now clamp to `max(_, 1)` / `max(_, 0)` to prevent negative-px emission during Stage Manager / split-screen resize storms. Round-1 finding [2] (WKWebView runtime integration test) ACCEPTED as out of scope — vreaderTests has no precedent for WKWebView rendering integration; structural tests pin the exact `!important` contract and post-merge device verification exercises the rendered behaviour. 3 new regression-guard tests (column-count !important at portrait + landscape viewports, tiny-viewport clamp) + updates to existing column-fill assertion. 30/30 EPUBPagination tests pass on iPhone 17 Pro Simulator. Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-537-epub-paged-two-column-audit.md`. GH: #537 |

| 169| AI Settings expanded sections (API Key / Provider Configuration / Data & Privacy) don't render after flipping toggle ON until app relaunch | Settings/AI | Medium | FIXED | **NOTE on numbering**: GH issue title says "Bug #167" because the verify-cron filing this didn't consult the local tracker — the EPUB rubber-band bug was already row #167. Assigning local row #169 (next available) and renaming the GH issue title to match. **Root cause**: `AISettingsViewModel.isAIEnabled` was a pure get/set computed property delegating to `FeatureFlags.isEnabled(.aiAssistant)` / `setOverride(_:for:)`. The `@Observable` macro only instruments stored properties — a computed property whose body reads/writes a non-Observable class bypasses `_$observationRegistrar` entirely on both read and write. Result: in `AISettingsSection`, the conditional `if viewModel.isAIEnabled { /* API Key, Provider Configuration, Data & Privacy */ }` never re-evaluated after the toggle's setter wrote through — SwiftUI didn't know to invalidate the view. The flag DID persist to UserDefaults; the conditional just didn't re-render. Only an app kill+relaunch re-initialized the view model from FeatureFlags on first render, picking up the new value. **Fix**: convert `isAIEnabled` from computed to stored property with a `didSet` write-through. Seed `self.isAIEnabled = featureFlags.isEnabled(.aiAssistant)` once at init time. The `@Observable` macro now instruments the stored property's storage — writes fire `_$observationRegistrar.withMutation`, reads call `_$observationRegistrar.access`, so SwiftUI's `if viewModel.isAIEnabled` block re-renders on the next runloop tick after toggle. The `oldValue != isAIEnabled` guard dedupes the WRITE-THROUGH (and resulting UserDefaults write) on same-value assignments. FeatureFlags' `Sendable` concurrency contract unchanged — fix is local to `AISettingsViewModel`. Codex MCP audit `019e13c8` (2 rounds): round 1 found 1 Medium (over-asserting test about `@Observable` same-value behavior — replaced with a sentinel-value UserDefaults test pinning the write-through dedup contract) + 1 Low (comment overclaim — rescoped to write-through, not re-renders); round 2 zero new findings, ship-as-is. Test gate: 3 new tests in `AISettingsViewModelTests` (`toggleNotifiesObservationTracker`, `toggleStillWritesThroughToFeatureFlags`, `idempotentSetIsNoOpAgainstFeatureFlags`) — 32/32 AISettings tests pass; 760/760 full unit suite green. Pre-FIXED verify per `.claude/rules/10-tdd.md` "Pure-logic bugs reproducible by a unit test: the RED→GREEN transition in Phase 3 already establishes Verify"; user-visible UI re-render is a mechanical consequence of the Observation contract pinned by the new test. **Residual note (NOT a regression)**: `AISettingsViewModel.hasConsent` has the same computed-property/non-observable shape. Currently only used as a `Toggle` binding (no conditional render block reads it), so no user-visible bug. If future UI conditionally renders off `viewModel.hasConsent`, it will need the same treatment. Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-500-ai-settings-no-rerender-on-toggle-audit.md`. GH: #500 |

| 159| EPUB highlights save to data layer but don't visually render on the page (CSS Highlight API not painting yellow background) | EPUB/*    | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED via two-part change addressing both the root cause and a latent issue surfaced during diagnosis**: (1) **XPath namespace rewrite in `resolveNodeFromXPath`** (root cause): EPUB chapters load as `application/xhtml+xml` so `documentElement.namespaceURI` is `http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml`. XPath 1.0 element names without a namespace prefix don't match XHTML-namespaced elements, so `getXPath`-produced paths like `/html/body/p[3]/text()[1]` returned null, `buildRange` returned null, and `__vreader_createHighlight` early-returned BEFORE either render path executed. Fix rewrites element-name segments to `*[local-name()="name"]` when document has a namespace; preserves `text()`, `comment()`, `node()` axis tokens; handles prefix-qualified names like `svg:svg` (Codex audit round-1 Medium fix). (2) **CSS Highlight API now primary, SVG Overlayer fallback** (visibility): even with valid Range, the SVG Overlayer paints rectangles in document coords into a 100%-tall SVG positioned over `<html>`. In paged EPUB mode (CSS multi-column layout), document y > viewport-height is clipped from the SVG's viewport even though the text appears in the next column visually — rect drawn but invisible. CSS Highlight API renders at text-paint time and follows column transforms automatically. Swapped the priority order. (3) **foliate-bridge.js DOMContentLoaded timing fix** (defensive): script is injected at `.atDocumentEnd` which runs AFTER DOMContentLoaded fires, so the auto-setup listener never executed and `window.__foliate.overlayer` stayed undefined. Replaced with `if (document.readyState === 'loading') addEventListener(...) else __vreader_setupFoliate()` so setup runs synchronously when past loading state. Codex MCP audit (thread `019e0c82`, 2 rounds): round 1 found 1 Medium (regex didn't handle prefix-qualified names) — fixed. Round 2 ship-as-is. Test gate: 748/748 unit tests pass. New regression-guard tests: 3 new in `EPUBHighlightBridgeTests` (`highlightAPIJS_rewritesXPathForXHTMLNamespace`, `highlightAPIJS_preservesNonElementSteps`, `highlightAPIJS_handlesPrefixedElementNames`) pinning the source-token markers for the namespace rewrite + prefix strip. Also fixed pre-existing stale test `txtFormat_canUseUnified_whenSettingIsUnified` from bug #158's #468 regression (renamed to `txtFormat_cannotUseUnified_evenWhenSettingIsUnified` and inverted to pin post-#158 contract). Pre-FIXED verify on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.117: opened mini-epub3.epub → Native EPUB mode → long-press on "testing" in paragraph 1 → custom VReader menu (Highlight \| Add Note \| Copy) → tap Highlight → **yellow background visibly painted on the word "testing"**, persists after dismissing selection state. Live state probe via DebugBridge eval: `cssHighlightCount: 1`, `styleEls: 1`, `overlayerChildren: 0` — CSS Highlight API path (primary post-fix) ran end-to-end. Artifact: `bug-159-prefixed-yellow-highlight-visible-20260509.png`. **Filed by verify cron 2026-05-09T18:44** during feature #11 (EPUB text highlighting and note-taking) round-3 verification of the deferred gesture-driven user-flow slice. Reproducible end-to-end on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.116 using bundled `mini-epub3.epub` in **Native EPUB mode**: open mini-epub3 → Native mode → Chapter One paginated → long-press the word "some" in paragraph 3 → iOS shows custom VReader menu (`Highlight \| Add Note \| Copy`) — tap **Highlight** → selection animation dismisses. **(A) Data layer works**: opening side panel → Highlights tab shows row "🟡 some" — the highlight IS persisted with yellow color tag. **(B) Visual render does NOT apply**: the word "some" appears with IDENTICAL styling to surrounding text — no yellow background, no underline, no visible color difference. Reproducible in BOTH Sepia theme (initial) AND Light theme (which should give the cleanest yellow contrast); also persists across book close + reopen. So the user gets ZERO visual feedback that their Highlight tap had any effect; the only way to verify is opening the Highlights tab manually. **Why this matters**: breaks feature #11's user-visible contract. Round-2 verified bridge-readiness (`__vreader_createHighlight` defined, `selectionChanged` registered, programmatic `CSS.highlights.set` round-trips). Round-3 closed the deferred gesture slice and discovered: while the bridge accepts the gesture-driven call AND data layer persists, the **paint pipeline does not fire** — highlight invisible to the user. Suspect surface (not yet code-read in detail): `EPUBHighlightBridge` (Swift message handler), `EPUBHighlightCoordinator` (Swift orchestration), `__vreader_createHighlight` (JS in WKWebView bundle), `CSS.highlights.set("vreader-highlight-<id>", new Highlight(range))` + a stylesheet rule like `::highlight(vreader-highlight-N) { background: yellow; }`. Possible root causes: (1) missing `::highlight(...)` CSS rule injection — `Highlight` registered in `CSS.highlights` but no stylesheet defines paint property; (2) JS path divergence — gesture menu uses different path than bridge probe, constructs Range incorrectly; (3) CSS theming conflict overriding background. Light theme reproduces too, so (3) is less likely. 4 screenshot artifacts (`bug-159-epub-highlight-not-rendered-sepia-20260509.png`, `bug-159-epub-highlight-not-rendered-light-20260509.png`, `bug-159-epub-highlight-not-rendered-after-reopen-20260509.png`, `bug-159-epub-highlight-data-persisted-20260509.png` showing the saved entry in Highlights tab). **Fix scope options**: (a) add `::highlight()` CSS rules to EPUB theme injection — smallest change if gap is purely CSS; (b) wire saved-highlight overlay paint via dedicated layer (matching how AZW3 highlight overlay restoration is "deferred to WI-7" per row 11); (c) wrap selected range in `<span class="vreader-highlight">` with explicit yellow styling instead of `CSS.highlights` — more invasive, more reliable across user agents. Cross-format check needed: Foliate (AZW3/MOBI) might have same gap; PDF and TXT/MD use different render paths. Affects every EPUB user trying to highlight text via the gesture-driven flow. Feature #11 VERIFIED gated on this fix. GH: #472 |

Plus a coalescing refactor to `LibraryViewModel.refresh(force:)`: the previous behavior dropped re-entrant calls (`guard !isRefreshing else { return }`); the new behavior drains pending work via `repeat { hasPendingRefresh = false; await loadBooks() } while hasPendingRefresh && iterations < 8`, with a follow-up `Task { @MainActor [weak self] in await self?.refresh(force: true) }` fallback if the 8-iteration safety bound trips. Either (a) EPUB text extraction for mini-epub3 produces empty content, (b) background indexer failed silently for EPUB books, or (c) search query path doesn't dispatch to the EPUB-indexed store. **Blocks**: feature #2 EPUB cross-chapter verification (no way to reach the result-tap step without populated results) AND bug #182 close-gate device verification (same precondition). Suspect surface: `ReaderSearchCoordinator.enqueueBookIndexing` / `BackgroundIndexingCoordinator` / EPUB text extractor. No silent-failure log output captured (`log show --predicate 'subsystem == "com.vreader.app"'` returns empty for the session). **FIXED 2026-05-14**: root cause was `BackgroundIndexingCoordinator.enqueueIndexing` scheduling its `processQueue()` work via `Task.detached(priority: .background) { [weak self] in await self?.processQueue() }`. Caller `ReaderSearchCoordinator.setup(...)` creates the coordinator as a local, awaits `enqueueBookIndexing(...)`, then returns — local reference drops and `[weak self]` allows the actor to be deallocated BEFORE the detached background task starts running. By task-start time, `self?` is nil and `processQueue` never runs. EPUB exposed this more than TXT because `EPUBParser.open(...)` + spine iteration + `parser.close()` adds enough delay before setup() returns that the coordinator dies before scheduling resolves; TXT happened to win the race more often (synchronous `Data(contentsOf:)` + smaller fixture). Fix: change `[weak self]` to strong `self` capture in the detached task. The actor's invariant ("we must drain pendingJobs once isProcessing flips true") makes strong-self correct — the task voluntarily releases the strong reference when `processQueue` returns. Regression test `enqueueIndexing_processesEvenWhenCallerDropsCoordinator` directly reproduces the bug: pre-fix `callCount == 0`, post-fix `callCount == 1`. Manual-fallback audit (Codex unavailable): `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-653-epub-indexer-actor-deallocates-audit.md`, verdict ship-as-is. GH: #653 |

| 183| TXT search panel freezes UI on first open — enqueueBookIndexing inherits @MainActor, calls TXTTextExtractor.extractWithOffsets (blocking file I/O + encoding detection) on main thread | Reader/TXT | Medium | FIXED | **Reported by user 2026-05-14**. Its synchronous extractor calls (`TXTTextExtractor.extractWithOffsets` → `decodeFile` → `Data(contentsOf:)` + `TXTService.decodeForDisplayAndSearch(data)`) have no internal `await`, so the whole call runs on MainActor until the next natural suspension. | 182| EPUB search: cross-chapter result tap navigates to chapter top but no yellow highlight visible — Locator.textQuote contained the raw search snippet (`...prefix<b>match</b>suffix...`), plain-text matcher couldn't find the literal HTML in the DOM (round 2: snippet-markup defect FIXED; round 3 needed for deferred-eval pipeline silence in user-tap flow) | Reader/EPUB | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-18 (round-3, GH #621)** — round-1 (defer JS to didFinish) and round-2 (`cleanSnippetForTextQuote` snippet-markup strip, below) both landed but the symptom persisted: verify-cron round-5 DOM-probes proved the `.vreader_search_highlight` span is never injected via the user-tap pipeline. Round-3 root cause — `EPUBHighlightBridge.searchHighlightJS` ran `window.find()` exactly once, synchronously at `webView(_:didFinish:)`; at that instant the freshly-loaded chapter has not finished its post-load relayout (foliate-js `cssPreprocessJS`, a `WKUserScript` injected `atDocumentEnd`, rewrites every `-epub-*`/`page-break-*` rule), so `window.find()` returns false and no span is created. The Swift stash→consume pipeline was already correct. **Fix** (JS-only, `searchHighlightJS`): poll `window.find()` on a bounded 50ms retry loop (40 attempts ≈ 2s) until the rendered DOM is searchable; a `window.__vreaderSearchHighlightGen` generation token supersedes concurrent retry loops; the wrap-and-insert is `try/catch`-guarded. 4 new structural unit tests in `EPUBHighlightBridgeTests`. Codex audit `019e3959` (3 rounds — 1 Medium + 4 Low all fixed — ship-as-is); audit log `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-621-epub-cross-chapter-highlight-r3-audit.md`. The retry's real runtime behavior isn't unit-testable; post-merge close-gate re-runs the cross-chapter search-tap repro with a `vreader-debug://eval?bridge=epub` DOM probe (CU-free) — `awaiting-device-verification`. — **FIXED 2026-05-15** (round-2 root cause) — the round-1 v3.21.50 deferred-eval mechanism (`pendingHighlightJS` stash + didFinish consume on the coordinator) was correct and remains in place. It was however *necessary but not sufficient*: the deferred JS was running cleanly against the new chapter DOM, but `window.find()` was always returning `false` because the search string passed to it was the raw display snippet from `SearchQueryExecutor.extractSnippet`, formatted as `"...prefix<b>match</b>suffix..."` for the search-results-list UI. `window.find()` is a plain-text DOM walker — it cannot match literal `<b>` tags or `...` ellipses against rendered text. PDFKit's `findString(_:withOptions:)` has the same plain-text contract, so PDF search-tap was silently broken the same way. **Fix** is at the resolver layer (`SearchHitToLocatorResolver.swift`): new `cleanSnippetForTextQuote(_:)` helper prefers the `<b>…</b>` bolded portion (the exact matched substring of the source text) and falls back to ellipsis + literal `<b>` / `</b>` stripping when the bold pair is missing, returning `nil` for inputs that collapse to whitespace. `resolveEPUB` / `resolvePDF` route their `hit.snippet` through it. TXT/MD resolvers are untouched (they use UTF-16 offsets, never `textQuote`). The fallback is deliberately narrow — `1 < 2 > 1` math notation, generics, etc. pass through verbatim. Codex audit `019e2c4d` (2 rounds, ship-as-is): round 1 found 3 Lows — over-broad `<...>` strip (replaced with targeted `<b>` / `</b>` only), missing edge tests (added 8 direct unit tests covering nil/empty/whitespace/empty-bold/lone-tag/math-notation), architectural snippet-vs-matchedText coupling (accepted as known limitation, filed as follow-up). Round 2 found 1 doc-drift Low (fixed). Test gate: 24/24 `SearchHitToLocatorResolverTests` pass, including 5 indirect-via-resolve tests + 8 direct `cleanSnippetForTextQuote` tests. Pre-FIXED verify: pure-logic bug reproducible by unit test → RED→GREEN transition is the Verify step per rule. Same-chapter highlight path unaffected by the resolver change (resolver runs once per search-result-tap regardless of chapter). Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-594-bug-182-search-snippet-strip-audit.md`. Round-1 history preserved below. — **REOPENED 2026-05-15** by verify-cron round-5 (`dev-docs/verification/feature-2-20260515-round5.md`, `result: fail`). DOM-probe verification via `vreader-debug://eval?bridge=epub` against installed v3.22.8 build 360 (which carries the bug #182 deferred-eval fix from v3.21.50): three probes at t≈0.8s, t≈2.3s, t≈5.3s post search-result-tap **all** return `document.querySelectorAll('.vreader_search_highlight').length === 0`. The DOM probe rules out the visual-capture-timing ambiguity that left round-4 inconclusive — the highlight span is never injected into the chapter-2 DOM at any point during the 3s window. Cross-chapter navigation itself works (`docTitle: "Chapter Two"`, `scrollTop: 0`, matched word in `<p>` #1) — only the highlight-JS injection path is silent. Round-1 hypothesis "stash gets cleared / not consumed by didFinish" was disproven by the round-2 trace: the deferred eval IS firing, `window.find()` IS being called, but it's looking for `...The quick brown <b>fox</b> jumps...` in a DOM that only contains the plain text `The quick brown fox jumps`. Evidence: `feature-2-r5-eval-epub-t5s-20260515.json` + `feature-2-r5-eval-epub-scrollstate-20260515.json` + 2 PNG artifacts. — **Reported by user 2026-05-14**. Same-chapter searches work; cross-chapter searches navigate correctly but show no highlight. `pendingHighlightJS` evaluated immediately after `webView.loadFileURL()` (async) in `updateUIView` — `window.find()` runs on old/loading page, fails silently. Fix: defer to `didFinish` like `pendingScrollFraction`. **FIXED 2026-05-14** (round 1, code-complete but runtime-incomplete per round-5): added `pendingHighlightJS` + `onPendingHighlightJSCompleted` stash fields to `EPUBWebViewBridge.Coordinator`. `updateUIView`'s URL-change branch now stashes the JS + completion onto the coordinator (mirroring the existing `pendingScrollFraction` pattern); `didFinish` consumes them after theme/pagination/scroll setup and before the persisted-highlights restore Task. The immediate-eval tail block gains two guards (`!urlIsChanging` AND coordinator's in-flight sentinel) so a mid-load updateUIView refresh doesn't double-fire window.find() against the still-loading DOM. Same-chapter highlight injection path (`EPUBReaderContainerView+Highlights`) preserved — URL stable, JS evals against already-loaded DOM unchanged. 6 unit tests on the coordinator stash fields (`EPUBWebViewBridgeCoordinatorPendingHighlightJSTests`); full deferred-eval cross-DOM round-trip needs device verification (post-merge `awaiting-device-verification` label). | 179| TXT reading content obscured by Dynamic Island — REOPENED for restore + chapter-nav. Real root cause: GeometryReader race makes `proxy.safeAreaInsets.top = 0` momentarily on initial render + chapter-nav rebuild → `textContainerInset.top = 16` (base only) → glyph lands behind DI | Reader/TXT | Medium | FIXED | **Filed by user 2026-05-14**. Same symptom as EPUB bug #163 (GH #487). Root cause: `ReaderContainerView.body` applies `.ignoresSafeArea(edges: .top)` to the format-specific reader views, then `TXTViewConfig.textInset.top = 16` is hardcoded with no safe-area compensation. **FIXED 2026-05-14** mirroring bug #163's EPUB pattern: (1) `TXTTextViewBridge` gains `safeAreaTopInset: CGFloat = 0` and a static helper `combinedTextInset(base:safeAreaTop:)` that returns `UIEdgeInsets(top: base.top + max(0, safeAreaTop), ...)`; `makeUIView`/`updateUIView` apply the combined inset to `textContainerInset`. (2) `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` gains the same `safeAreaTopInset` param and applies it to `tableView.contentInset.top` with `contentInsetAdjustmentBehavior = .never`. (3) `TXTReaderContainerView` wraps all 3 bridge call sites (`readerContent`, `chapterReaderContent`, `chunkedReaderContent`) in `GeometryReader { proxy in Bridge(safeAreaTopInset: proxy.safeAreaInsets.top, ...) }`. Adding OR subtracting `topInset` would move it WORSE. Symptom is real but root cause must be elsewhere: investigate (a) `UIScrollView.contentInsetAdjustmentBehavior` interaction with SwiftUI `.ignoresSafeArea(edges: .top)`, (b) `safeAreaInsets` on the textView stacking atop `textContainerInset.top`, (c) `attemptScrollRestore` racing another code path that resets `contentOffset` post-call, (d) save/restore asymmetry — `scrollViewDidScroll` recording position with inset folded in vs `charOffsetToScrollOffset` returning un-folded coord. Bugfix-cron 2026-05-15 iteration applied the row-directed fix, ran Codex, reverted before commit, deleted branch unmerged. **FIXED 2026-05-15 (v3.21.62)** by a follow-on bugfix-cron iteration with a different root-cause diagnosis: `ReaderSafeAreaResolver` static helper feeds `topInsetWithFallback(proxy.safeAreaInsets.top)` instead of the raw proxy value to all 3 TXT bridges + the MD bridge, bridging the GeometryReader-vs-makeUIView race via `UIWindow.safeAreaInsets.top` lookup (same escape pattern bug #73 used in `ReaderChromeBar.windowSafeAreaTop`). | 225| **Numbering note (2026-05-19)**: this row keeps 225; GH #910 (the `TTSService.rate` recursion bug) was filed concurrently and also titled itself "Bug #225" — that colliding row was renumbered to 226. This row (GH #911, TXT test-isolation) is the canonical Bug #225. `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` is test-isolation-broken — `observeLocator()` registers a global `NotificationCenter` observer with `object: nil`, so when Swift Testing runs the 5 sibling tests in the suite in parallel each test's `.readerPositionDidChange` posts bleed into every other test's fire-counter; the `observer.count() == 1` assertion in `openSeedsRestoredPosition` fails (`count → 5`, or higher under a full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` run) | Tests/Reader | Low | FIXED | **Filed by bugfix-cron 2026-05-19** while fixing Bug #180 / GH #614. Confirmed PRE-EXISTING on `origin/main` (`42908c4`): running `-only-testing:vreaderTests/TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` on a clean `main` worktree fails identically (`Expectation failed: (observer.count() → 5) == 1` at `TXTReaderViewModelTests.swift:501`). Not caused by the Bug #180 change — the #180 diff touches no test-broadcast code. **Root cause**: `observeLocator()` (`TXTReaderViewModelTests.swift:382`) does `NotificationCenter.default.addObserver(forName: .readerPositionDidChange, object: nil, ...)`. `TXTReaderViewModel.broadcastPosition` posts `.readerPositionDidChange` with `object:` = the `Locator` (not the VM). Swift Testing executes the 5 `@Test`s in `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` concurrently by default; each test's `vm.open()` / `updateScrollPosition` posts on the shared global center, and every test's observer (filtering `object: nil`) counts them all. `openSeedsRestoredPosition`'s round-2-audit `#expect(observer.count() == 1)` therefore sees the sibling tests' posts. The 3 capture-only tests pass because they assert on the most-recent `captured` locator, not the count. **Why it surfaced now**: Bug #180 added 7 new test files; some (`TXTReaderViewModelContinuousTests`) call `updateScrollPosition` many times, increasing the global `.readerPositionDidChange` traffic in the parallel pool and making the pre-existing race lose more reliably under `-only-testing:vreaderTests`. **Not a product defect** — `broadcastPosition`'s runtime behavior (post exactly once on restore) is correct; the *test* cannot observe "exactly once" because it has no per-VM filter. **Fix direction**: give `observeLocator()` a way to scope to one VM's posts — e.g. make the suite serialized (`@Suite(.serialized)`) so sibling posts don't interleave, OR have `broadcastPosition` post with `object:` = a per-VM token the observer can filter on, OR pass the expected fingerprint and count only locators whose `bookFingerprint` matches. Lowest-risk is `.serialized` on the suite. Other suspected sibling flakes in the same full-run failure set (`ReaderPositionServiceTests`, `PDFReaderViewModel - Position Service` debounce/coalesce tests) are load-dependent timing flakes — pass in isolation, fail under full-suite CPU contention — distinct from this isolation bug; not filed (known timing-flake class). **2nd instance — same root cause, same suite:** `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` (`preplant_partialSuccess_notifiesForLandedRowsOnly`, `preplant_postsBookFileStateDidChange_perRow`) fails identically in isolation on `origin/main` — its `BookFileStateDidChange`-notification capture's `receivedKeys` is polluted with duplicate + cross-fingerprint keys from the suite's other parallel tests (same global-`NotificationCenter` + parallel-`@Suite` race). `progress_movesMonotonically_through3Phases` in the same suite is intermittently affected. Same `@Suite(.serialized)` fix applies. Tracked under this row to avoid bug-row proliferation; both suites need the serialized-suite fix. **FIXED 2026-05-19** (branch `fix/issue-911-txt-test-isolation`): the documented `.serialized`-only direction was tried first and **empirically proved insufficient** — running the suites with `@Suite(.serialized)` applied still produced cross-test pollution (`observer.count() → 7`; `receivedKeys` captured 10 keys including sibling-test fingerprints). The shipped fix instead makes each capturing observer **filter deterministically by a globally-unique discriminator**, immune to Swift Testing's parallel scheduling: (1) `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` — `observeLocator(for:)` filters captured posts by the posting `Locator.bookFingerprint`, and each of the 5 broadcast tests mints its own unique fingerprint via `uniqueFingerprint()` (UUID-derived 64-char SHA); (2) `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` — the two `preplant_*` tests mint entries from `makeUniqueEPUBBytes()` (UUID-salted bytes → globally-unique `fingerprintKey`) and observe through `observePreplant(expectedKeys:)`, which records only posts whose key is in the test's own set. A sibling's posts carry different keys/fingerprints and are dropped. `.serialized` is kept on both suites as cheap defense-in-depth + documented intent (matching the bug #213 `BookSourceHTTPClient` precedent). **Test-only fix** — no production code touched (`broadcastPosition` / `postPreplantNotifications` runtime behavior was already correct). **RED** confirmed on base `b504d9d`: both suites fail deterministically under parallel mode (`TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` → `count → 7`; `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` → both `preplant_*` polluted). **GREEN**: both fixed suites pass 14/14, **3 consecutive deterministic runs** under default parallel mode; neighbour-regression run of 7 suites (the 2 fixed + 5 `TXTReaderViewModel*`) passes 40/40. Full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` gate was environmentally blocked (4 attempts, iOS Simulator test host repeatedly failing to bootstrap — `Test crashed with signal kill before establishing connection` — under concurrent-agent simulator contention; a fresh sim reboot did not clear it); a test-only 2-file change with both suites + 5 neighbours green cannot regress the rest of the suite (other tests compile against unchanged production code + unchanged test helpers). Codex audit `019e3f8f`, 1 round, ship-as-is — `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-911-txt-test-isolation-audit.md` (1 Low finding fixed: added an exact-cardinality assertion to `preplant_postsBookFileStateDidChange_perRow`). GH: #911 |

Added an additive `ignoringKeyboardElements` option to `auditCurrentScreen` (+ `isSystemKeyboardChrome` vertical-band classifier — the QuickType strip sits flush *above* `app.keyboards`' frame, so strict containment misses it); the two search-sheet tests opt in. | 222| `ReaderSettingsStore.autoPageTurnInterval` infinite recursion — its `didSet` re-assigns the property to clamp it, which under `@Observable` re-enters the synthesized setter forever → stack overflow (`EXC_BAD_ACCESS`) | Reader/Settings | Medium | FIXED | **Filed by bugfix-cron 2026-05-19** while fixing Bug #221 / GH #849 — discovered as the *second* root cause of #221's flaky full-suite test-host crash. `ReaderSettingsStore` is `@Observable @MainActor`. `autoPageTurnInterval`'s `didSet` body did `autoPageTurnInterval = max(1.0, min(60.0, autoPageTurnInterval))` to clamp. The `@Observable` macro rewrites a `didSet`-bearing stored property into a computed `autoPageTurnInterval` over backing `_autoPageTurnInterval`; the `didSet` lives on `_autoPageTurnInterval`. The body's `autoPageTurnInterval = …` therefore calls the **computed** setter → sets `_autoPageTurnInterval` → fires `didSet` again — Swift's didSet-self-assignment suppression does not span the computed→stored boundary, so it recurses unboundedly. Crash report `vreader-2026-05-19-084307.ips`: `Thread stack size exceeded due to excessive recursion`, faulting thread `com.apple.main-thread`. **A product defect, not test-only**: `applyResolvedSettings` (per-book settings, bug #84) assigns `autoPageTurnInterval` when a per-book interval differs from the global → crashes the app at runtime. The recursion does not fire during `init` (Swift suppresses observers there). Sibling `backgroundOpacity` already uses the correct pattern — explicit `get`/`set` over a private `_backgroundOpacity`, clamping in `set`. **FIXED 2026-05-19** (PR — branch `fix/issue-849-vreadertests-suite-crash`, same PR as Bug #221): `autoPageTurnInterval` converted to a computed `get`/`set` pair over a private `_autoPageTurnInterval`, clamping in `set` — no `didSet`, no observer re-entry; `init` assigns the backing var directly. 4 regression tests in `ReaderSettingsStoreTests` (in-range + same-value post-init assignment = the tightest recursion repro; clamping; persistence round-trip). Codex audit: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-849-vreadertests-suite-crash-audit.md`. GH: #882 |

Mirrors the Bug #209 root-cause-(C) fix on `ReaderSettingsPanel`/`AnnotationsPanelView`. **Investigation note**: applying the same modifier from the *parent* (on the `SearchView` instance in `ReaderContainerView+Sheets.swift`) instead crashed the app at runtime — stacking `.accessibilityElement` over a subtree already terminating in `.accessibilityIdentifier` is the crash; placing it inside `SearchView` paired with its own identifier does not. A runtime accessibility-tree dump confirmed `app.otherElements["searchSheet"]` now resolves to exactly one `Other` container with the 5 children carrying their own correct identifiers (`magnifyingglass`/`searchTextField`/`searchCancelButton`/`searchEmptyPromptView`). Harness redesign, not a one-liner — candidate for the feature #45 verification-harness sweep. **FIXED 2026-05-20** (bugfix-cron, branch `fix/845-debugbridge-epub-highlight-driver`): shipped the EPUB counterpart of PR #1047's TXT/MD highlight-driver. Reuses the existing `vreader-debug://highlight?start=<int>&end=<int>[&color=<name>]` URL grammar — when an EPUB is the active reader, a new DEBUG-only observer (`EPUBReaderContainerView+DebugBridgeHighlight.swift`) receives the `.debugBridgeHighlightCommand` notification, evaluates `EPUBDebugBridgeHighlightJS.buildResolveRangeJS(...)` in the active EPUB WKWebView (resolved via `DebugReaderRegistry.shared.epubWebView(for:token:)`), and persists via the same `HighlightCoordinator.create(locator:anchor:selectedText:color:)` entry the gesture path uses in `EPUBReaderContainerView+Highlights.handleHighlightAction`. The JS walks visible text nodes in document order (skipping `data-vreader-decoration` bilingual siblings — XPath-parity with `EPUBHighlightJS.selectionTrackingJS`), maps `[start, end)` UTF-16 offsets to a DOM `EPUBSerializedRange`, snaps surrogate-pair boundaries forward/backward to surround full scalars, rejects whitespace-only selections to match gesture semantics, and returns the range to Swift. Paint happens via the production renderer pipeline (`HighlightCoordinator.create` → `EPUBHighlightRenderer.apply(record:)` → `EPUBHighlightActions.createHighlightJS(for: record)` → `__vreader_createHighlight(record.highlightId.uuidString, ...)`) with the canonical persisted UUID — no transient JS-side ID can leak onto the live page. The observer also re-validates `(fingerprintKey, token, webView, currentHref)` after the `evaluateJavaScript` round-trip so a reader-close or chapter-nav that races the completion drops the stale result instead of persisting against the new chapter. `Feature11EPUBHighlightVerificationTests` rewritten to drive both methods through `bridgeHelper.highlight(start:10, end:30, color:nil)` — replacing the long-press gesture probe with the harness — and assert via the existing Highlights-tab `highlightsEmptyState` disappearance + reopen-persistence checks. `VerificationDebugBridgeHelper` gained a `highlight(start:end:color:)` method + matching `DebugCommand.highlightURL(...)` builder. Test gate: 6828 tests in 682 suites green (35.4s, iPhone 17 Pro Sim iOS 26.4). Codex audit `019e4485-37a1-7f60-bf86-dca766483924`, 2 rounds — Round 1 surfaced 1 High (transient-ID lifecycle) + 3 Medium (stale-async state, surrogate-pair snapping, whitespace-only selection) all fixed; Round 2 zero findings; final verdict `ship-as-is`. Verification: `Feature11EPUBHighlightVerificationTests` is the natural verification harness — it's also the awaiting-device-verification slice. GH: #845 |

| 217| `ReplacementTransform` regex rules silently no-op under load — `applyRegexRule` blocks on a 1s `DispatchSemaphore` over `DispatchQueue.global()`; a saturated dispatch pool misfires the timeout and the replacement returns the input unchanged | Services/TextMapping | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-18 by bugfix-cron** while running the Bug #216 / GH #838 `/fix-issue` full `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests` gate. `ReplacementTransform.applyRegexRule` (`vreader/Services/TextMapping/ReplacementTransform.swift:134-170`) dispatches the regex match to `DispatchQueue.global()` and blocks the caller on `DispatchSemaphore.wait(timeout: 1.0)`. When the global dispatch pool is saturated (full parallel Swift Testing suite, ~750 concurrent tests), the work item can't get a thread within 1s → `waitResult == .timedOut` → `matches = []` → the rule returns the input unchanged, silently skipping the replacement. Two trivial-regex tests fail under the full parallel suite: `ReplacementTransformTests.regex_multipleMatches` (`\d+`→`#` on "page 1 of 100" → got "page 1 of 100" unchanged) and `replace_regex_groupCapture` (`(\w+)@(\w+)`→`$2/$1` on "user@domain" → got "user@domain" unchanged); both pass in isolation. **Two-fold impact**: (1) test-gate reliability — the 2 regex tests flaky-fail every full parallel run; (2) latent production correctness — content replacement rules can silently no-op in-app whenever the dispatch pool is briefly saturated. Concurrency hazard: `DispatchSemaphore.wait()` blocks the calling thread; when that caller is a Swift Concurrency cooperative-pool thread the block can starve the pool. **Fix direction**: drop the dispatch-semaphore timeout (trivial-pattern replacement is microsecond-scale; guard catastrophic backtracking at rule-creation time instead) or use a structured-concurrency `Task` with real cancellation — do not block a cooperative thread on a semaphore. **FIXED 2026-05-18** (bugfix-cron, branch `fix/issue-839-replacementtransform-regex-noop`): `applyRegexRule` now calls `regex.matches(in:options:range:)` synchronously on the calling thread — the `DispatchQueue.global()` + 1s `DispatchSemaphore` timeout machinery and the `regexTimeoutSeconds` constant are removed. The dispatch hop bought nothing (content-replacement matching is microsecond-scale); the timeout was itself the bug, only weakly protective (the caller was blocked up to 1s anyway, and `DispatchWorkItem.cancel()` cannot preempt a running `regex.matches`), and untested. RED→GREEN: a new opt-in contention test `regexRule_appliesUnderGlobalQueueContention` (CPU-saturates `DispatchQueue.global()`) FAILED on the pre-fix commit (regex no-op'd → input returned unchanged) and PASSES post-fix; all 15 `ReplacementTransformTests` green. The contention test is `.enabled(if: env VREADER_RUN_CONTENTION_TESTS=="1")` — gated out of normal runs because a faithful pool-starvation repro must CPU-saturate the default-QoS pool and is antisocial to the parallel scheduler. Codex audit `019e3769`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is. Residual (accepted): a pathological user-authored regex is no longer apply-time-bounded — the removed timeout was only weakly protective; a real guard belongs at rule-creation-time pattern validation, not apply-time. GH: #839 |

RED→GREEN verified under the parallel scheduler: pre-fix `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/PDFViewBridgeThemeTests` logged 72 `_raiseExceptionForBackgroundThreadLayerPropertyModification` off-main backtraces; post-fix logged 0, all 8 tests pass (per-test time 0.44-0.55s → 0.003-0.010s). | 211| EPUB tap-on-highlight shows no inline Delete menu — feature #53 WI-4 `click`-listener hit-test uses the wrong `Range.compareBoundaryPoints` constant, so every in-range tap misses | Reader/EPUB | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-17 by verify-cron** during feature #53 round-5 EPUB device verification on iPhone 17 Pro Max Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.27.15 (build 429). Tapping a yellow EPUB highlight never surfaces the inline "Delete Highlight" menu (feature #53 criterion (a)) — the tap toggles reader chrome instead. Reproduced 3× incl. with a deliberately large unambiguous tap target. **Root cause (confirmed via DebugBridge `eval`):** `vreader/Views/Reader/EPUBHighlightJS.swift` WI-4 `click` listener calls `range.compareBoundaryPoints(Range.END_TO_START, probe)` intending to test `range.end >= probe.start`, but `END_TO_START` compares `range`'s *start* to `probe`'s *end* — it should be `Range.START_TO_END`. A replayed hit-test (caret at offset 102 inside a highlight Range spanning offsets 97–107, same text node) returned `startVsProbe=-1, endVsProbe=-1, hit=false`. The JS registry, CSS Highlight paint, and `caretPositionFromPoint` are all intact and the `click` event fires (verified via an injected counter) — only the membership comparison is wrong, so no `highlightTapHandler` message posts and `.readerHighlightTapped` never fires. Blocks feature #53 criterion (c) / VERIFIED for EPUB. Detail in Open Bug Details. Evidence: `dev-docs/verification/feature-53-20260517-round5.md`. **FIXED 2026-05-17** (verify-cron → fix-issue, same session): one-token fix in `EPUBHighlightJS.swift` — the WI-4 `click`-listener end-boundary check now uses `range.compareBoundaryPoints(Range.START_TO_END, probe)` (was `END_TO_START`); per the DOM spec `START_TO_END` compares `range`'s end to `probe`'s start, which is the comparison the membership test needs. Regression-guard test `EPUBHighlightTapBridgeJSTests.highlightAPIJS_tapHitTest_comparesEndBoundaryAgainstTapPoint` pins the correct call expression. Codex audit thread `019e34d6`, 1 round, ship-as-is. Pre-FIXED verify: installed the fixed build, opened the `mini-epub3` EPUB, ran a DebugBridge `eval` of the membership predicate against synthetic ranges in the live WebView — fixed `START_TO_END` → in-range probe `hit:true`, out-of-range `hit:false`; old `END_TO_START` → in-range `hit:false` (reproduces the bug). | 205| UIEditMenuInteraction logs Error on `presentEditMenu(with:)` — TXT tap-on-highlight menu still invisible after Bug #203 coord-space fix shipped (likely UITextView own-edit-menu conflict OR add+present timing) | Reader/TXT, Reader/* | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-17** in branch `fix/issue-751-uieditmenuinteraction-weak-delegate` (PR pending). Both verify-cron root-cause hypotheses (UITextView own-edit-menu conflict; add+present timing) were wrong. Real root cause confirmed from the iOS 26.5 SDK header: `UIEditMenuInteraction` declares `delegate` as a **weak** property (`@property (nonatomic, weak, nullable, readonly) id<UIEditMenuInteractionDelegate> delegate;`). `UIKitHighlightActionPresenter.present` created its `PresenterDelegate` as a local with no owning reference, so the delegate deallocated the instant `present` returned; UIKit then asynchronously composed the menu, queried a now-nil delegate, found no menu, and logged `<compose failure>`. **Fix**: the delegate is associated onto the `UIEditMenuInteraction` object itself (`objc_setAssociatedObject`, `OBJC_ASSOCIATION_RETAIN_NONATOMIC`) — the interaction, strongly retained by the host view, owns its delegate, so the delegate lives exactly as long as the interaction. This binds the lifetime to the interaction rather than the presenter, which matters because the reader containers build `UIKitHighlightActionPresenter()` inline in `body` and `TXTTextViewBridge.updateUIView` rebinds it on every SwiftUI render (an earlier presenter-holds-delegate fix would have been a flaky race — caught by the Codex audit). `present` also sweeps any prior presenter-installed edit-menu interaction off the view (keyed on the association, so the text view's own built-in menu is untouched). RED→GREEN: 4 tests in `UIKitHighlightActionPresenterTests` — `interaction.delegate` reads non-nil after `present` (the weak property proves retention), interaction installed on the host view, two `present` calls supersede rather than accumulate, unrelated edit-menu interactions survive the sweep. Codex audit `019e345b`, 3 rounds, ship-as-is — round 1 caught the ephemeral-presenter race (High) + weak test seam, round 2 caught the abort-path linger (Medium) + a comment-policy-name Low, round 3 clean. Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-751-uieditmenuinteraction-weak-delegate-audit.md`. **Filed by verify-cron 2026-05-16** during Bug #203 / Feature #53 round-3 device verification on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.5) at v3.23.9 (commit cfab8c5, build 386 — fresh post-WI-1 install). Repro: `vreader-debug://reset` → seed war-and-peace → tap card → reader opens at chapter 1 page 2/4 → long-press "Prince" → custom menu (Highlight/Add Note/Define/▶) → tap Highlight → "Prince" yellow + `snapshot.highlightCount: 1` ✓ → dismiss selection via neutral tap (chrome toggles off, consistent) → tap on yellow "Prince" → **NO inline edit/delete menu**. Bug #202 chrome-toggle suppression IS active (tap-on-highlight short-circuits before chrome-toggle fall-through). Bug #203 coord-space fix shipped (sourceRect is now textView-local). But the menu still doesn't appear. **Evidence**: iOS log subsystem `[com.apple.UIKit:EditMenuInteraction]` reports `Error`-level events correlated with each tap-on-yellow attempt (06:37:06.411 + 06:37:35.673 from `xcrun simctl spawn booted log show --predicate 'process == "vreader"'`). Message body privacy-redacted (`<compose failure [shared UUID]>`) but severity + subsystem confirm UIKit is rejecting the `presentEditMenu(with:)` call. **Suspect root cause** (code-read at `HighlightActionPresenter.swift:118-124`): (a) UITextView already owns a built-in `UIEditMenuInteraction` for its selection menu; for the TXT non-chunked path the `view` passed to `present(for:in:)` IS the HighlightableTextView, and adding a SECOND UIEditMenuInteraction to a UITextView may conflict with the system one. (b) Synchronous `view.addInteraction(interaction)` + `interaction.presentEditMenu(with: cfg)` in the same call may not give UIKit a runloop tick to integrate the interaction into the responder chain — Apple sample code sometimes dispatches present to next main-queue cycle. **Fix direction**: prefer (a) — pass `textView.superview` or a reader-container view to `present(for:in:)` so the menu hosts on a view without an existing UIEditMenuInteraction; the sourceRect (already textView-local) gets converted to the host's coord space same shape as the chunked path's existing wrapper. (b) as cheaper backup if (a) doesn't address it. **Affects**: Feature #53 acceptance criterion (a) for TXT — round-3 device verify is `partial`. Likely also MD (same TXT bridge), EPUB (webView host — may NOT have the conflict, needs verification), PDF (pdfView host — same question). Foliate uses `.zero` sourceRect, separately tracked. Bug #203 close-gate verify is now `partial`/`fail` for this distinct second issue. GH: #751 |

The non-chapter path at line 131-133 (`readerContent`) is the only TXT path that wires `updatePagination` → `pageNavigator` via `TextReaderUIState.updatePagination` (line 90-110). The auto-page-turn guard in `TextReaderUIState.updateAutoPageTurner` (line 113-123): `guard enabled, isPagedMode, let nav = pageNavigator else { autoPageTurner?.stop(); return }` — when `pageNavigator` is nil (chapter branch), the turner is `.stop()`ed immediately. War-and-peace has chapter detection → `chapterReaderContent` active → `pageNavigator` nil → timer never fires. Affects every chaptered TXT file (the dominant real-book case). **Side observation**: `AutoPageTurner.pause()` is called from `.readerContentTapped` / `.readerNextPage` / `.readerPreviousPage` in `TXTReaderContainerView.swift:334-356`, but `AutoPageTurner.resume()` is never called anywhere in production (only `ttsService.resume()` + `URLSessionDownloadTask.resume()` exist). Once paused by any tap, timer stays paused until the toggle is OFF/ON cycled — may warrant follow-up; not the root cause of this bug. 5 screenshot artifacts saved (`feature-31-r3-reader-open-t0-20260509.png`, `feature-31-r3-reader-t8s-no-tap-20260509.png`, `feature-31-r3-reader-t14s-no-tap-20260509.png`, plus earlier `feature-31-r3-t0-19pct-20260509.png` + `feature-31-r3-t8s-20260509.png` + `feature-31-r3-t12s-toolbar-hidden-20260509.png`). **Fix scope options**: (a) wire `pageNavigator` into `chapterReaderContent` (paginate per chapter; AutoPageTurner advances within chapter and crosses chapter boundaries via the existing chapter navigation API) — most user-faithful, real engineering. (c) document + accept; track as feature-class follow-up. PDF/EPUB/AZW3 already capability-gated out by #156. MD reader likely has the same shape but needs a chaptered-MD fixture to verify. GH: #461 |
| 227| `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests.case11b` fails deterministically — `awaitReaderSettled` throws `.settleTimeout` immediately on a same-key reopen | DevTools/* | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-19 by the feature #55 (tap-on-annotated-text note preview) implementation run** during the WI-5 full-suite test gate. `case11b_sameKeyReopen_oldUnregisterCancelsOnlyOwnWaiter()` fails **deterministically** — 3/3 isolated runs of the `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests` suite — and fails **fast** (~0.06s, far under the test's 2.0s timeout budget), so `registry.awaitReaderSettled(for:token:timeout:2.0)` is throwing `DebugReaderProbeError.settleTimeout` *immediately* rather than resolving when probe B's `markReaderSettled` fires. **Repro**: `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests` on iPhone 17 Pro Sim — `case11b` records an issue at `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests.swift:169` (`Caught error: .settleTimeout`); the suite's other 5 tests pass. **Analysis**: the test registers probe A (token A) then probe B (token B) on the same key, spawns a `Task` that unregisters A at +50ms then `markReaderSettled(token: B)` at +100ms, and `await`s `awaitReaderSettled(token: B, timeout: 2.0)`. The fast `.settleTimeout` means either (1) A's `unregister(probeA)` is wrongly cancelling B's pending waiter — the exact regression the test guards against, in `vreader/Services/DebugBridge/DebugReaderRegistry+Settle.swift`'s unregister/cancel bookkeeping — or (2) the same-key reopen path mis-tracks B's waiter so `markReaderSettled(token: B)` never resolves it. **Scope**: discovered by feature #55's WI-5 test gate; feature #55 touches **zero** DebugBridge files — pre-existing, independent defect, filed per the working agreement (discover-a-bug → file, don't fix in an unrelated PR). **Severity Medium** — DebugBridge is DEBUG-only (not in Release), but a broken `awaitReaderSettled` undermines `vreader-debug://settle` and verification-harness reliability. **Root cause (2026-05-19)**: NOT a production bug — a **test-isolation defect**. The three settle suites (`DebugReaderRegistrySettle{Core,EdgeCase,Cleanup}Tests`) all drove the `DebugReaderRegistry.shared` **singleton** via `shared.reset()`. Swift Testing runs `@Test` methods in parallel; `case11b` keeps a `settleWaiter` suspended ~100ms (background `Task` unregisters A at +50ms, marks B settled at +100ms). During that window a *concurrent* test's `shared.reset()` wipes `settleWaiters` and resumes `case11b`'s waiter with a spurious `.settleTimeout`. The issue's two hypotheses are both wrong — the production `awaitReaderSettled`/`markReaderSettled`/`clearSettleState`/`unregister` same-key-reopen bookkeeping is correct (confirmed: `-parallel-testing-enabled NO` → all 6 cleanup tests pass; the "3/3 isolated runs" used a suite-level filter that still parallelizes all 6 methods). **Fix**: added DEBUG-only `DebugReaderRegistry.makeIsolatedForTests()` factory; the three settle suites' `makeRegistry()` now construct a fresh isolated instance per test — no shared mutable state, deterministic under parallelism. **Verified**: 3 settle suites (17 tests) pass 3/3 in parallel; `case11b` resolves in ~0.10s via B's mark. Codex audit `ship-as-is`. GH: #932 |
| 229| AZW3/MOBI highlight deleted via the Annotations panel is not stripped from the rendered Foliate overlay until reload | Reader/* | Medium | FIXED | **Numbering note (2026-05-19)**: this row was renumbered 228 → 229. GH #938 and GH #939 were filed concurrently by two different agents and BOTH titled themselves "Bug #228", colliding two rows in this file. Resolved per the #225/#226 collision precedent — the colliding row that an active `/fix-issue` run is working (GH #939, the `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests` singleton-isolation bug) keeps 228; this row (GH #938, the AZW3/MOBI Foliate overlay-strip bug) takes the next free number 229. The GH #938 issue title still reads "Bug #228" — `docs/bugs.md` is the source of truth and now says 229. **Filed 2026-05-19 by the feature #55 WI-7 (tap-on-annotated-text note preview, EPUB+Foliate wiring) implementation run** + confirmed by the WI-7 Gate-4 Codex audit (`019e3f25` round 1). Deleting an AZW3/MOBI (Foliate-rendered) highlight from the **Annotations panel** (Highlights tab → swipe-delete) removes it from persistence and the panel list, but the **rendered annotation overlay stays painted** in the reader until the next book reload. **Root cause**: the Foliate JS overlay strip (`FoliateHighlightRenderer.removeAnnotationJS(cfi:)` → `readerAPI.deleteAnnotation`) is driven by the `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` notification, which carries a **CFI**; `FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator` observes it and evaluates the JS strip on the live WKWebView. The panel swipe-delete (`HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight`) posts `.readerHighlightRemoved`, whose object is only the highlight **UUID string** — no CFI — and the Foliate Coordinator does not observe `.readerHighlightRemoved`. `removeHighlight` also deletes the `HighlightRecord` from persistence *before* posting, so a post-hoc `fetchHighlights` cannot recover the deleted record's CFI. The Foliate restore path (`FoliateSpikeView+Restore.swift`) only *adds* annotations (idempotent) and never reconciles removals. **Pre-existing latent gap** — the panel-delete path never posted `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete`, even before #55 — **surfaced by feature #55 WI-7**, which re-homed the AZW3/MOBI highlight tap to the #55 note preview and dropped the legacy #53 tap-time delete menu (`FoliateHighlightTapHandlerModifier.performDelete`, the only former producer of `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete`). After WI-7 the panel is the only delete path for AZW3/MOBI highlights, so the gap is now user-observable on the only supported path. EPUB is unaffected — `EPUBReaderContainerView` observes `.readerHighlightRemoved` and strips its WKWebView highlight via `HighlightCoordinator.handleRemoval` / `EPUBHighlightBridge.removeHighlightJS`. **Repro**: open an AZW3/MOBI book, create a highlight, swipe-delete it in the Annotations panel Highlights tab → highlight gone from the panel list but its colored overlay still painted in the reader; close+reopen the book → overlay now gone. **Fix direction**: plumb the CFI to the Foliate strip on a panel-delete — either (a) `HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight` captures the record's `.epub` anchor CFI before the persistence delete and posts `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` (cfi + fingerprintKey) alongside `.readerHighlightRemoved` (reuses the existing dormant Foliate observer — kept intentionally post-WI-7 as this hook), or (b) the Foliate host maintains a `[UUID: CFI]` cache populated as highlights restore/create and consults it on `.readerHighlightRemoved`. (a) is smaller but touches shared #53 highlight infrastructure; (b) keeps the change Foliate-local. **Severity Medium** — AZW3/MOBI-only, a stale visual that self-corrects on reload; persistence is correct, no data loss. **FIXED 2026-05-20** (branch `fix/issue-938-foliate-panel-delete-overlay-strip`): applied fix-direction (a) — `HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight` now captures the pre-delete record from `self.highlights` (the authoritative in-memory copy after `loadHighlights`), extracts the `.epub` anchor CFI via a new `private static epubAnchorCFI(of:)` helper that mirrors `FoliateHighlightJSBridge.cfi(from:)` (treats `nil` record, `nil` / non-`.epub` / empty-CFI anchor as no-CFI), and posts `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` with `["cfi": String, "fingerprintKey": String]` userInfo alongside the existing `.readerHighlightRemoved` (UUID). **Emission order** mirrors `FoliateHighlightJSBridge.delete` — `.readerHighlightRemoved` first (panel/list sync), then `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` (SVG overlay strip); a regression test pins this order. **Atomicity**: a persistence-delete throw posts neither notification — guarantees the overlay never strips a still-persisted highlight. **RED**: new `HighlightListViewModelFoliateOverlayStripTests` 6-test suite covered the epub-anchored happy path (with strict ordering assertion), pre-delete CFI capture, `.text`-anchor skip, nil-anchor skip, empty-CFI skip, and persistence-failure atomicity — failed 4× on pre-fix RED, passed 6/6 post-GREEN. **Verified GREEN**: focused suite 6/6, full `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests` 6811/6811 in 35.6s, deterministic. Production-code change is 26 lines (1 helper, 1 if-let post site) in `HighlightListViewModel.swift`; test file split per Gate-4 round 1 Low ("file size") into `HighlightListViewModelFoliateOverlayStripTests.swift`. Codex audit `019e43cf`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is (`.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-938-foliate-panel-delete-overlay-strip-audit.md`). **Note on the panel UI caller**: `HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight` has no current production UI caller (the `HighlightsSheet` cards expose `onJump` only, no swipe-delete affordance) — the bug filer correctly identified this VM as the future panel-delete entry point per their root-cause analysis; the fix lands the notification contract so that whenever the panel-delete UI lands the overlay strip works on day 1. The in-reader popover delete (`FoliateHighlightMutator.deleteHighlight` → `FoliateHighlightJSBridge.delete`) was already correct; this fix brings the latent panel path to the same contract.
